Here is the complete, verified catalog of every prototype-pollution defense pattern used across the Node.js core `lib/` directory.

---

## Prototype Pollution Defenses in Node.js Core (`lib/`)

> **Repo:** nodejs/node · **Commit:** `5b5f069a` (HEAD → main)  
> **Scope:** all `lib/` JS source files, excluding tests and benchmarks

---

### Architectural Foundation

Everything flows from two files loaded by the C++ bootstrap layer **before any user code can run**:

| File | Role |
|------|------|
| `lib/internal/per_context/primordials.js` | Captures every built-in method reference at VM startup; defines all Safe* wrappers |
| `lib/internal/util.js` | Exports shared frozen constants (`kEmptyObject`, `kEnumerableProperty`, `filterOwnProperties`, `setOwnProperty`) |

The ESLint rule `node-core/prefer-primordials` enforces that all other `lib/` files use the aliased forms (`ObjectAssign`, `ArrayPrototypePush`, etc.) rather than raw globals, making the protection systematic rather than ad-hoc.

---

## Pattern 1 — Null-Prototype Objects: `{ __proto__: null }` / `ObjectCreate(null)`

**What it prevents:** Any object inheriting from `Object.prototype` carries `toString`, `valueOf`, `hasOwnProperty`, `__defineGetter__`, etc. as inherited keys. An attacker-controlled key `"__proto__"` or `"constructor"` can silently walk up the chain. A null-prototype object has no chain at all.

**Canonical forms:**
```js
// Object literal — preferred modern form
const obj = { __proto__: null };

// Factory form — used when returned from a function
const obj = ObjectCreate(null);   // ObjectCreate = Object.create, captured in primordials
```

**Scale: 156 files** contain at least one usage. Representative examples:

| File | Lines | Context |
|------|-------|---------|
| `lib/internal/modules/c

"'use strict';\n\n/* eslint-disable node-core/prefer-primordials */\n\n// This file subclasses and stores the JS builtins that come from the VM\n// so that Node.js's builtin modules do not need to later look these up from\n// the global proxy, which can be mutated by users.\n\n// Use of primordials have sometimes a dramatic impact on performance, please\n// benchmark all changes made in performance-sensitive areas of the codebase.\n// See: https://github.com/nodejs/node/pull/38248\n\nconst {\n  defineProperty: ReflectDefineProperty,\n  getOwnPropertyDescriptor: ReflectGetOwnPropertyDescriptor,\n  ownKeys: ReflectOwnKeys,\n} = Reflect;\n\n// `uncurryThis` is equivalent to `func => Function.prototype.call.bind(func)`.\n// It is using `bind.bind(call)` to avoid using `Function.prototype.bind`\n// and `Function.prototype.call` after it may have been mutated by users.\nconst { apply, bind, call } = Function.prototype;\nconst uncurryThis = bind.bind(call);\nprimordials.uncurryThis = uncurryThis;\n\n// `applyBind` is equivalent to `func => Function.prototype.apply.bind(func)`.\n// It is using `bind.bind(apply)` to avoid using
